{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01U2ARBBPHTVSSNaataYG4g3","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→/*\n     2→Copyright 2015 The Kubernetes Authors.\n     3→\n     4→Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \"License\");\n     5→you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\n     6→You may obtain a copy of the License at\n     7→\n     8→    http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\n     9→\n    10→Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\n    11→distributed under the License is distributed on an \"AS IS\" BASIS,\n    12→WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\n    13→See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\n    14→limitations under the License.\n    15→*/\n    16→\n    17→// Package leaderelection implements leader election of a set of endpoints.\n    18→// It uses an annotation in the endpoints object to store the record of the\n    19→// election state. This implementation does not guarantee that only one\n    20→// client is acting as a leader (a.k.a. fencing).\n    21→//\n    22→// A client only acts on timestamps captured locally to infer the state of the\n    23→// leader election. The client does not consider timestamps in the leader\n    24→// election record to be accurate because these timestamps may not have been\n    25→// produced by a local clock. The implemention does not depend on their\n    26→// accuracy and only uses their change to indicate that another client has\n    27→// renewed the leader lease. Thus the implementation is tolerant to arbitrary\n    28→// clock skew, but is not tolerant to arbitrary clock skew rate.\n    29→//\n    30→// However the level of tolerance to skew rate can be configured by setting\n    31→// RenewDeadline and LeaseDuration appropriately. The tolerance expressed as a\n    32→// maximum tolerated ratio of time passed on the fastest node to time passed on\n    33→// the slowest node can be approximately achieved with a configuration that sets\n    34→// the same ratio of LeaseDuration to RenewDeadline. For example if a user wanted\n    35→// to tolerate some nodes progressing forward in time twice as fast as other nodes,\n    36→// the user could set LeaseDuration to 60 seconds and RenewDeadline to 30 seconds.\n    37→//\n    38→// While not required, some method of clock synchronization between nodes in the\n    39→// cluster is highly recommended. It's important to keep in mind when configuring\n    40→// this client that the tolerance to skew rate varies inversely to master\n    41→// availability.\n    42→//\n    43→// Larger clusters often have a more lenient SLA for API latency. This should be\n    44→// taken into account when configuring the client. The rate of leader transitions\n    45→// should be monitored and RetryPeriod and LeaseDuration should be increased\n    46→// until the rate is stable and acceptably low. It's important to keep in mind\n    47→// when configuring this client that the tolerance to API latency varies inversely\n    48→// to master availability.\n    49→//\n    50→// DISCLAIMER: this is an alpha API. This library will likely change significantly\n    51→// or even be removed entirely in subsequent releases. Depend on this API at\n    52→// your own risk.\n    53→package leaderelection\n    54→\n    55→import (\n    56→\t\"bytes\"\n    57→\t\"context\"\n    58→\t\"fmt\"\n    59→\t\"sync\"\n    60→\t\"time\"\n    61→\n    62→\t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/api/errors\"\n    63→\tmetav1 \"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/apis/meta/v1\"\n    64→\t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/runtime\"\n    65→\t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/wait\"\n    66→\trl \"k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/resourcelock\"\n    67→\t\"k8s.io/klog/v2\"\n    68→\t\"k8s.io/utils/clock\"\n    69→)\n    70→\n    71→const (\n    72→\tJitterFactor = 1.2\n    73→)\n    74→\n    75→// NewLeaderElector creates a LeaderElector from a LeaderElectionConfig\n    76→func NewLeaderElector(lec LeaderElectionConfig) (*LeaderElector, error) {\n    77→\tif lec.LeaseDuration <= lec.RenewDeadline {\n    78→\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"leaseDuration must be greater than renewDeadline\")\n    79→\t}\n    80→\tif lec.RenewDeadline <= time.Duration(JitterFactor*float64(lec.RetryPeriod)) {\n    81→\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"renewDeadline must be greater than retryPeriod*JitterFactor\")\n    82→\t}\n    83→\tif This implementation does not guarantee that only one\n// client is acting as a leader (a.k.a. fencing).\n//\n// A client only acts on timestamps captured locally to infer the state of the\n// leader election. The client does not consider timestamps in the leader\n// election record to be accurate because these timestamps may not have been\n// produced by a local clock. The implemention does not depend on their\n// accuracy and only uses their change to indicate that another client has\n// renewed the leader lease. Thus the implementation is tolerant to arbitrary\n// clock skew, but is not tolerant to arbitrary clock skew rate.\n//\n// However the level of tolerance to skew rate can be configured by setting\n// RenewDeadline and LeaseDuration appropriately. The tolerance expressed as a\n// maximum tolerated ratio of time passed on the fastest node to time passed on\n// the slowest node can be approximately achieved with a configuration that sets\n// the same ratio of LeaseDuration to RenewDeadline. For example if a user wanted\n// to tolerate some nodes progressing forward in time twice as fast as other nodes,\n// the user could set LeaseDuration to 60 seconds and RenewDeadline to 30 seconds.\n//\n// While not required, some method of clock synchronization between nodes in the\n// cluster is highly recommended. It's important to keep in mind when configuring\n// this client that the tolerance to skew rate varies inversely to master\n// availability.\n//\n// Larger clusters often have a more lenient SLA for API latency. This should be\n// taken into account when configuring the client. The rate of leader transitions\n// should be monitored and RetryPeriod and LeaseDuration should be increased\n// until the rate is stable and acceptably low. It's important to keep in mind\n// when configuring this client that the tolerance to API latency varies inversely\n// to master availability.\n//\n// DISCLAIMER: this is an alpha API. This is measured against time of\n\t// last observed ack.\n\t//\n\t// A client needs to wait a full LeaseDuration without observing a change to\n\t// the record before it can attempt to take over. When all clients are\n\t// shutdown and a new set of clients are started with different names against\n\t// the same leader record, they must wait the full LeaseDuration before\n\t// attempting to acquire the lease. Thus LeaseDuration should be as short as\n\t// possible (within your tolerance for clock skew rate) to avoid a possible\n\t// long waits in the scenario.\n\t//\n\t// Core clients default this value to 15 seconds.\n\tLeaseDuration time.Duration\n\t// RenewDeadline is the duration that the acting master will retry\n\t// refreshing leadership before giving up.\n\t//\n\t// Core clients default this value to 10 seconds.\n\tRenewDeadline time.Duration\n\t// RetryPeriod is the duration the LeaderElector clients should wait\n\t// between tries of actions.\n\t//\n\t// Core clients default this value to 2 seconds.\n\tRetryPeriod time.Duration\n\n\t// Callbacks are callbacks that are triggered during certain lifecycle\n\t// events of the LeaderElector\n\tCallbacks LeaderCallbacks\n\n\t// WatchDog is the associated health checker\n\t// WatchDog may be null if it's not needed/configured.\n\tWatchDog *HealthzAdaptor\n\n\t// ReleaseOnCancel should be set true if the lock should be released\n\t// when the run context is cancelled. The core components are:\\n\\n**Main Execution Flow** (`leaderelection.go`):\\n- The `LeaderElector` struct drives the election process through three main phases:\\n  1. **Acquisition Phase** (`acquire()`): Candidates attempt to acquire the lease with retry logic (RetryPeriod)\\n  2. **Leadership Phase** (`renew()`): The leader continuously renews its lease before the RenewDeadline expires\\n  3. **Release Phase** (`release()`): Optional graceful step-down of leadership\\n\\n- The `Run()` method orchestrates these phases, calling `acquire()` first, then delegating to `renew()` which loops with `tryAcquireOrRenew()`\\n- Failover detection relies on `LeaseDuration`: non-leaders wait for the full lease expiration before attempting acquisition. If a leader fails to renew within `RenewDeadline`, it automatically loses leadership\\n\\n**Lease Locking Mechanism** (`resourcelock/leaselock.go`):\\n- The `LeaseLock` type implements Get/Create/Update operations against Kubernetes Lease resources\\n- The `LeaderElectionRecord` (defined in `interface.go`) stores:\\n  - `HolderIdentity`: The current leader's identity\\n  - `LeaseDurationSeconds`: How long the lease remains valid\\n  - `LeaderTransitions`: Counter tracking leadership changes (enabling detection of churn)\\n  - `AcquireTime` and `RenewTime`: Timestamps for validating lease expiration\\n\\n**Re-election Mechanism**:\\n- When a leader becomes unavailable, its lease expires after `LeaseDuration` seconds\\n- Candidates check if the observed lease is still valid via `isLeaseValid()` which compares current time against stored RenewTime\\n- If invalid, `tryAcquireOrRenew()` increments `LeaderTransitions` and attempts to take over\\n- The `maybeReportTransition()` method fires the `OnNewLeader` callback when leadership changes\\n\\n### etcd: Raft-Based Leader Election\\n\\netcd uses **Raft consensus protocol** for leader election, implemented in the etcdserver subsystem:\\n\\n**Main Server Integration** (`server/etcdserver/server.go`):\\n- The `EtcdServer` struct manages the cluster and contains Raft integration\\n- The `run()` method creates a `raftReadyHandler` that handles leadership state changes via callbacks:\\n  - `updateLead()`: Tracks the current leader ID\\n  - `updateLeadership()`: Handles transitions between leader and follower states\\n  - When becoming leader, it records `leadElectedTime`, resumes compaction, and notifies via `leaderChanged` channel\\n  - When losing leadership, it demotes the lessor and pauses compaction\\n\\n- The `ensureLeadership()` function validates leadership during critical operations:\\n  - Checks if the member is still actively receiving heartbeats (`isActive()`)\\n  - Performs a linearizable read to confirm current leadership status\\n  - Used to prevent stale leaders from performing operations (addresses etcd issue #15247)\\n\\n**Raft Node Management** (`server/etcdserver/raft.go`):\\n- The `raftNode` struct wraps the go.etcd.io/raft library for consensus\\n- The `start()` method runs the core election loop:\\n  - Monitors `Ready()` channel for rd.SoftState.Lead`\\n  - Tracks current Raft state: `islead = rd.RaftState == raft.StateLeader`\\n\\n**Failover & Re-election Mechanism**:\\n- **Automatic Detection**: When a leader fails, Raft followers detect missing heartbeats (based on `TickMs` timeout)\\n- **Leader Change**: Followers with up-to-date logs become candidates and win election through Raft's voting mechanism\\n- **State Synchronization**: Followers receive snapshots and entries from the new leader, ensuring data consistency\\n- **Metrics Tracking**: The code increments `leaderChanges` counter on transitions, sets `hasLeader` and `isLeader` metrics\\n\\n### Key Differences\\n\\n| Aspect | Kubernetes | etcd |\\n|--------|-----------|------|\\n| **Mechanism** | Lease-based (optimistic locking) | Raft consensus (voting-based) |\\n| **Failover Detection** | Lease expiration after LeaseDuration | Heartbeat timeout (TickMs) |\\n| **Re-election Trigger** | Manual acquisition when lease expired | Automatic via Raft election |\\n| **Coordination** | API server (Lease resources) | In-cluster consensus |\\n| **Consistency Guarantee** | Best-effort (tolerates clock skew) | Strong (Raft guarantees) |\\n| **Fencing** | Not guaranteed (can have multiple leaders briefly) | Guaranteed single leader (Raft) |\\n\\nBoth approaches provide leader election suitable for their architectures: Kubernetes leverages etcd\\n\\n### Kubernetes: Lease-Based Leader Election\\n\\nKubernetes implements leader election through a **lease-based coordination mechanism** located in `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/`. The core components are:\\n\\n**Main Execution Flow** (`leaderelection.go`):\\n- The `LeaderElector` struct drives the election process through three main phases:\\n  1. **Acquisition Phase** (`acquire()`): Candidates attempt to acquire the lease with retry logic (RetryPeriod)\\n  2. **Leadership Phase** (`renew()`): The leader continuously renews its lease before the RenewDeadline expires\\n  3. **Release Phase** (`release()`): Optional graceful step-down of leadership\\n\\n- The `Run()` method orchestrates these phases, calling `acquire()` first, then delegating to `renew()` which loops with `tryAcquireOrRenew()`\\n- Failover detection relies on `LeaseDuration`: non-leaders wait for the full lease expiration before attempting acquisition. If a leader fails to renew within `RenewDeadline`, it automatically loses leadership\\n\\n**Lease Locking Mechanism** (`resourcelock/leaselock.go`):\\n- The `LeaseLock` type implements Get/Create/Update operations against Kubernetes Lease resources\\n- The `LeaderElectionRecord` (defined in `interface.go`) stores:\\n  - `HolderIdentity`: The current leader's identity\\n  - `LeaseDurationSeconds`: How long the lease remains valid\\n  - `LeaderTransitions`: Counter tracking leadership changes (enabling detection of churn)\\n  - `AcquireTime` and `RenewTime`: Timestamps for validating lease expiration\\n\\n**Re-election Mechanism**:\\n- When a leader becomes unavailable, its lease expires after `LeaseDuration` seconds\\n- Candidates check if the observed lease is still valid via `isLeaseValid()` which compares current time against stored RenewTime\\n- If invalid, `tryAcquireOrRenew()` increments `LeaderTransitions` and attempts to take over\\n- The `maybeReportTransition()` method fires the `OnNewLeader` callback when leadership changes\\n\\n### etcd: Raft-Based Leader Election\\n\\netcd uses **Raft consensus protocol** for leader election, implemented in the etcdserver subsystem:\\n\\n**Main Server Integration** (`server/etcdserver/server.go`):\\n- The `EtcdServer` struct manages the cluster and contains Raft integration\\n- The `run()` method creates a `raftReadyHandler` that handles leadership state changes via callbacks:\\n  - `updateLead()`: Tracks the current leader ID\\n  - `updateLeadership()`: Handles transitions between leader and follower states\\n  - When becoming leader, it records `leadElectedTime`, resumes compaction, and notifies via `leaderChanged` channel\\n  - When losing leadership, it demotes the lessor and pauses compaction\\n\\n- The `ensureLeadership()` function validates leadership during critical operations:\\n  - Checks if the member is still actively receiving heartbeats (`isActive()`)\\n  - Performs a linearizable read to confirm current leadership status\\n  - Used to prevent stale leaders from performing operations (addresses etcd issue #15247)\\n\\n**Raft Node Management** (`server/etcdserver/raft.go`):\\n- The `raftNode` struct wraps the go.etcd.io/raft library for consensus\\n- The `start()` method runs the core election loop:\\n  - Monitors `Ready()` channel for state transitions\\n  - Detects leader changes via `rd.SoftState.Lead` from the Raft layer\\n  - Determines new leadership: `newLeader := rd.SoftState.Lead != raft.None && rh.getLead() != rd.SoftState.Lead`\\n  - Tracks current Raft state: `islead = rd.RaftState == raft.StateLeader`\\n\\n**Failover & Re-election Mechanism**:\\n- **Automatic Detection**: When a leader fails, Raft followers detect missing heartbeats (based on `TickMs` timeout)\\n- **Leader Change**: Followers with up-to-date logs become candidates and win election through Raft's voting mechanism\\n- **State Synchronization**: Followers receive snapshots and entries from the new leader, ensuring data consistency\\n- **Metrics Tracking**: The code increments `leaderChanges` counter on transitions, sets `hasLeader` and `isLeader` metrics\\n\\n### Key Differences\\n\\n| Aspect | Kubernetes | etcd |\\n|--------|-----------|------|\\n| **Mechanism** | Lease-based (optimistic locking) | Raft consensus (voting-based) |\\n| **Failover Detection** | Lease expiration after LeaseDuration | Heartbeat timeout (TickMs) |\\n| **Re-election Trigger** | Manual acquisition when lease expired | Automatic via Raft election |\\n| **Coordination** | API server (Lease resources) | In-cluster consensus |\\n| **Consistency Guarantee** | Best-effort (tolerates clock skew) | Strong (Raft guarantees) |\\n| **Fencing** | Not guaranteed (can have multiple leaders briefly) | Guaranteed single leader (Raft) |\\n\\nBoth approaches provide leader election suitable for their architectures: Kubernetes leverages
